<p><b>John Tyler</b> (March 29, 1790 – January 18, 1862) was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_the_United_States" title="List of Presidents of the United States">tenth</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a> (1841–1845). He was elected <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">vice president</a> on the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1840" title="United States presidential election, 1840">1840</a> <a href="/wiki/Whig_Party_(United_States)" title="Whig Party (United States)">Whig</a> ticket with <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Harrison" title="William Henry Harrison">William Henry Harrison</a>, and became president after his <a href="/wiki/Running_mate" title="Running mate">running mate</a>'s death in April 1841. Tyler was known as a supporter of <a href="/wiki/States%27_rights" title="States' rights">states' rights</a>, which endeared him to his fellow <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginians</a>, yet his acts as president showed that he was willing to support nationalist policies as long as they did not infringe on the rights of the states. Still, the circumstances of his unexpected rise to the presidency and his possible threat to the ambitions of other potential presidential candidates left him estranged from both major parties in Washington. A firm believer in <a href="/wiki/Manifest_destiny" title="Manifest destiny">manifest destiny</a>, President Tyler sought to strengthen and preserve the Union through <a href="/wiki/United_States_territorial_acquisitions" title="United States territorial acquisitions">territorial expansion</a>, most notably the annexation of the independent <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Texas" title="Republic of Texas">Republic of Texas</a> in his last days in office.</p>
<p>Tyler, born to <a href="/wiki/Tyler_family" title="Tyler family" class="mw-redirect">an aristocratic Virginia family</a>, came to national prominence at a time of political upheaval. In the 1820s the nation's only political party, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic-Republican_Party" title="Democratic-Republican Party">Democratic-Republicans</a>, split into factions. Though initially a <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_Democratic_Party" title="History of the United States Democratic Party">Democrat</a>, his opposition to <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Jackson" title="Andrew Jackson">Andrew Jackson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martin_Van_Buren" title="Martin Van Buren">Martin Van Buren</a> led him to ally with the Whig Party. Tyler served as a Virginia <a href="/wiki/Virginia_House_of_Delegates" title="Virginia House of Delegates">state legislator</a>, <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Virginia" title="Governor of Virginia">governor</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">U.S. representative</a>, and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">U.S. senator</a> before his election as vice president in the presidential election of 1840. He was <a href="/wiki/Ticket_balance" title="Ticket balance">put on the ticket</a> to attract states' rights Southerners to what was then a Whig coalition to defeat Van Buren's re-election bid.</p>
<p>Harrison's death made Tyler the first vice president to <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_line_of_succession" title="United States presidential line of succession">succeed to the presidency</a> without being elected to the office. To forestall constitutional uncertainty, Tyler immediately took the <a href="/wiki/Oath_of_office_of_the_President_of_the_United_States" title="Oath of office of the President of the United States">oath of office</a>, moved into the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a>, and assumed full presidential powers, a precedent that would govern future successions and eventually become codified in the <a href="/wiki/Twenty-fifth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Twenty-fifth Amendment to the United States Constitution">Twenty-fifth Amendment</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Strict_constructionism" title="Strict constructionism">strict constructionist</a>, Tyler found much of the Whig platform <a href="/wiki/Constitutionality" title="Constitutionality">unconstitutional</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Veto" title="Veto">vetoed</a> several of his party's bills. Believing that the president should set policy instead of deferring to Congress, he attempted to bypass the Whig establishment, most notably Kentucky Senator <a href="/wiki/Henry_Clay" title="Henry Clay">Henry Clay</a>. Most of Tyler's <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_States" title="Cabinet of the United States">Cabinet</a> resigned soon into his term, and the Whigs, dubbing him <i>His Accidency</i>, expelled him from the party. Though Tyler was not the first President to veto bills, he was the first to see his veto overridden by Congress. Although he faced a stalemate on domestic policy, he had several foreign-policy achievements, including the <a href="/wiki/Webster%E2%80%93Ashburton_Treaty" title="Webster–Ashburton Treaty">Webster–Ashburton Treaty</a> with <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">Britain</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Wanghia" title="Treaty of Wanghia">Treaty of Wanghia</a> with <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing China</a>.</p>
<p>President Tyler dedicated his last two years in office to the <a href="/wiki/Texas_annexation" title="Texas annexation">annexation of Texas</a>. He initially sought election to a full term, but after losing the support of both Whigs and Democrats, he withdrew. In the last days of his term, Congress passed the resolution authorizing the Texas annexation, which was carried out by Tyler's successor, <a href="/wiki/James_K._Polk" title="James K. Polk">James K. Polk</a>. When the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> began in 1861, Tyler sided with the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederate</a> government, and won election to the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_the_Confederate_States" title="Congress of the Confederate States">Confederate House of Representatives</a> shortly before his death. Although some have praised Tyler's political resolve, his presidency is generally held in <a href="/wiki/Historical_rankings_of_United_States_Presidents" title="Historical rankings of United States Presidents" class="mw-redirect">low esteem by historians</a>; today he is considered an obscure president, with little presence in the American cultural memory.<sup id="cite_ref-legacy_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-legacy-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>
